MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourceslblMAX_DATA.TextMax Data
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourceslinkLabel1.ToolTipThe 3DR Radios have 2 status LEDs, one red and one green. green LED blinking - searching for another radio green LED solid - link is established with another radio red LED flashing - transmitting data red LED solid - in firmware update mode
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRTXPOWER.ToolTipTXPOWER is the transmit power in dBm. 20dBm is 100mW. It is useful to set this to lower levels for short range testing.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRNETID.ToolTipNETID is a 16 bit 'network ID'. This is used to seed the frequency hopping sequence and to identify packets as coming from the right radio. Make sure you use a different NETID from anyone else running the same sort of radio in the area.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourceslabel12.TextRSSI
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesAIR_SPEED.ToolTipAIR_SPEED is the inter-radio data rate in rounded kbps. So 128 means 128kbps. Max is 192, min is 2. I would not recommend values below 16 as the frequency hopping and tdm sync times get too long.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesOPPRESEND.ToolTipOPPRESEND enables/disables "opportunistic resend". When enabled the radio will send a packet twice if the serial input buffer has less than 256 bytes in it. The 2nd send is marked as a resend and discarded by the receiving radio if it got the first packet OK. This makes a big difference to the link quality, especially for uplink commands.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesECC.ToolTipECC is to enable/disable the golay error correcting code. It defaults to off. If you enable it then you packets take twice as many bytes to send, so you lose half your air bandwidth, but it can correct up to 3 bit errors per 12 bits of data. Use this for long range, usually in combination with a lower air data rate. The golay decode takes 20 microsecond per transmitted byte (40 microseconds per user data byte) which means you will also be a bit CPU constrained at the highest air data rates. So you usually use golay at 128kbps or less.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRSSI.ToolTipsee the spec for a RSSI to dBm graph. The numbers at the end are: txe: number of transmit errors (eg. transmit timeouts) rxe: number of receive errors (crc error, framing error etc) stx: number of serial transmit overflows rrx: number of serial receive overflows ecc: number of 12 bit words successfully corrected by the golay code which result in a valid packet CRC

MissionPlanner.Controls.MavCommandSelection.resourceslabel1.TextYou can add MAVLink commands to the command selection of Planner View's Mission Grid. To add a command, you have to know the ID. The name will automatically be filled out if the ID is already defined in the MAVLink libraries. You can also add an ID that is not yet defined. In this case, you have to give the name as well. Adding a command here does not mean that the autopilot will accept or execute it. So you have to know what you are doing.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourceslinkLabel1.ToolTipThe 3DR Radios have 2 status LEDs, one red and one green. green LED blinking - searching for another radio green LED solid - link is established with another radio red LED flashing - transmitting data red LED solid - in firmware update mode
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRTXPOWER.ToolTipTXPOWER is the transmit power in dBm. 20dBm is 100mW. It is useful to set this to lower levels for short range testing.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRNETID.ToolTipNETID is a 16 bit 'network ID'. This is used to seed the frequency hopping sequence and to identify packets as coming from the right radio. Make sure you use a different NETID from anyone else running the same sort of radio in the area.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourceslabel12.TextRSSI
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesAIR_SPEED.ToolTipAIR_SPEED is the inter-radio data rate in rounded kbps. So 128 means 128kbps. Max is 192, min is 2. I would not recommend values below 16 as the frequency hopping and tdm sync times get too long.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesOPPRESEND.ToolTipOPPRESEND enables/disables "opportunistic resend". When enabled the radio will send a packet twice if the serial input buffer has less than 256 bytes in it. The 2nd send is marked as a resend and discarded by the receiving radio if it got the first packet OK. This makes a big difference to the link quality, especially for uplink commands.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesROPPRESEND.ToolTipOPPRESEND enables/disables "opportunistic resend". When enabled the radio will send a packet twice if the serial input buffer has less than 256 bytes in it. The 2nd send is marked as a resend and discarded by the receiving radio if it got the first packet OK. This makes a big difference to the link quality, especially for uplink commands.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesECC.ToolTipECC is to enable/disable the golay error correcting code. It defaults to off. If you enable it then you packets take twice as many bytes to send, so you lose half your air bandwidth, but it can correct up to 3 bit errors per 12 bits of data. Use this for long range, usually in combination with a lower air data rate. The golay decode takes 20 microsecond per transmitted byte (40 microseconds per user data byte) which means you will also be a bit CPU constrained at the highest air data rates. So you usually use golay at 128kbps or less.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRECC.ToolTipECC is to enable/disable the golay error correcting code. It defaults to off. If you enable it then you packets take twice as many bytes to send, so you lose half your air bandwidth, but it can correct up to 3 bit errors per 12 bits of data. Use this for long range, usually in combination with a lower air data rate. The golay decode takes 20 microsecond per transmitted byte (40 microseconds per user data byte) which means you will also be a bit CPU constrained at the highest air data rates. So you usually use golay at 128kbps or less.

MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesMAX_FREQ.ToolTipmaximum frequency in kHz
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRSSI.ToolTipsee the spec for a RSSI to dBm graph. The numbers at the end are: txe: number of transmit errors (eg. transmit timeouts) rxe: number of receive errors (crc error, framing error etc) stx: number of serial transmit overflows rrx: number of serial receive overflows ecc: number of 12 bit words successfully corrected by the golay code which result in a valid packet CRC
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesGPO1_1R_COUT.ToolTipOPPRESEND enables/disables "opportunistic resend". When enabled the radio will send a packet twice if the serial input buffer has less than 256 bytes in it. The 2nd send is marked as a resend and discarded by the receiving radio if it got the first packet OK. This makes a big difference to the link quality, especially for uplink commands.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRRTSCTS.ToolTipEnable or disable Hardware flow control
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesMAVLINK.ToolTipAIR_SPEED is the inter-radio data rate in rounded kbps. So 128 means 128kbps. Max is 192, min is 2. I would not recommend values below 16 as the frequency hopping and tdm sync times get too long.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesTXPOWER.ToolTipTXPOWER is the transmit power in dBm. 20dBm is 100mW. It is useful to set this to lower levels for short range testing.
MissionPlanner.Radio.Sikradio.resourcesRTSCTS.ToolTipEnable or disable Hardware flow control

MissionPlanner.Swarm.WaypointLeader.WPControl.resourcestextBox1.TextHow to Use: 1. connect all drones including masters (right click top icon bar "connection options") 2. select the correct vehicle and click set ground master 3. select the correct vehicle and click set air master 4. upload the path to the air master drone. 5. set the seperation and lead options 6. allow all drones to get gps lock, and calibrate. (failing to do so means they might fail prearm checks, this could be tested beforhand to ensure smooth operation) 7. ensure your ground master is ready and waiting on the flight path 8. click start
